<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(July 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guam" title="Music of Guam">Music of Guam</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Guam" title="Culture of Guam">Culture of Guam</a></div>
<p>Post-European-contact <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">Chamorro</a> Guamanian culture is a combination of American, Spanish, Filipino, other Micronesian Islander and Mexican traditions, with few remaining indigenous pre-Hispanic customs. These influences are manifested in the local language, music, dance, sea navigation, cuisine, fishing, games (such as batu, chonka, estuleks, and bayogu), songs and fashion. During Spanish colonial rule (1668–1898) the majority of the population was converted to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> and religious festivities such as Easter and Christmas became widespread. Post-contact Chamorro cuisine is largely based on corn, and includes tortillas, tamales, atole and chilaquiles, which are a clear influence from Spanish trade between Mesoamerica and Asia. The modern <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">Chamorro language</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian_language" title="Malayo-Polynesian language">Malayo-Polynesian language</a> with much Spanish influence. Many Chamorros also have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_name" title="Spanish name">Spanish surnames</a> because of their conversion to Roman Catholic Christianity and the adoption of names from the <a href="/wiki/Cat%C3%A1logo_alfab%C3%A9tico_de_apellidos" title="Catálogo alfabético de apellidos">Catálogo alfabético de apellidos</a>, a phenomenon also common to the Philippines and Latin America.</p>
<p>Due to foreign cultural influence from Spain, most aspects of the early indigenous culture have been lost, though there has been a resurgence in preserving any remaining pre-Hispanic culture in the last few decades. Some scholars have traveled throughout the Pacific Islands conducting research to study what the original Chamorro cultural practices such as dance, language, and canoe building may have been like.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puntan_Dos_Amantes_(Guam)_-_DSC01150.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG/220px-Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG/330px-Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG/440px-Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puntan_Dos_Amantes_(Guam)_-_DSC01150.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Puntan Dos Amantes</i> ("Two Lovers Point"), a <a href="/wiki/National_Natural_Landmark" title="National Natural Landmark">National Natural Landmark</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPS_PdA_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPS_PdA-31">[31]</a></sup> well known for its romantic associations</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Two aspects of indigenous pre-Hispanic culture that withstood time are chenchule' and inafa'maolek. Chenchule' is the intricate system of reciprocity at the heart of Chamorro society. It is rooted in the core value of inafa'maolek. Historian Lawrence Cunningham in 1992 wrote, "In a Chamorro sense, the land and its produce belong to everyone. <span lang="cha"><a href="/wiki/Inafa%27maolek" title="Inafa'maolek">Inafa'maolek</a></span>, or interdependence, is the key, or central value, in Chamorro culture ... <span lang="cha">Inafa'maolek</span> depends on a spirit of cooperation and sharing. This is the armature, or core, that everything in Chamorro culture revolves around. It is a powerful concern for mutuality rather than <a href="/wiki/Individualism" title="Individualism">individualism</a> and private property rights."</p>
<p>The core culture or Pengngan Chamorro is based on complex social protocol centered upon respect: From sniffing over the hands of the elders (called mangnginge in Chamorro), the passing down of legends, chants, and courtship rituals, to a person asking for permission from spiritual ancestors before entering a jungle or ancient battle grounds. Other practices predating Spanish conquest include <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">galaide'</a> canoe-making, making of the <a href="/wiki/Belembaotuyan" title="Belembaotuyan">belembaotuyan</a> (a string musical instrument made from a gourd), fashioning of <i><span lang="cha">åcho' atupat</span></i> slings and slingstones, tool manufacture, <span lang="cha"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=M%C3%A5tan_Guma%27&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Måtan Guma' (page does not exist)">Måtan Guma'</a></span> burial rituals, and preparation of herbal medicines by <a href="/wiki/Suruhanu" title="Suruhanu">Suruhanu</a>.</p>
<p>Master craftsmen and women specialize in weavings, including plaited work (<a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">niyok</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Pandanus" title="Pandanus">åkgak</a>-leaf baskets, mats, bags, hats, and food containments), loom-woven material (<a href="/wiki/Plumeria" title="Plumeria">kalachucha-hibiscus</a> and banana fiber skirts, belts and burial shrouds), and body ornamentation (bead and shell necklaces, bracelets, earrings, belts and combs made from tortoise shells and <a href="/wiki/Spondylus" title="Spondylus">Spondylus</a>).</p>
<p>The cosmopolitan and multicultural nature of modern Guam poses challenges for Chamorros struggling to preserve their culture and identity amidst forces of acculturation. The increasing numbers of Chamorros, especially Chamorro youth, relocating to the U.S. Mainland has further complicated both definition and preservation of Chamorro identity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> While only a few masters exist to continue traditional art forms, the resurgence of interest among the Chamorros to preserve the language and culture has resulted in a growing number of young Chamorros who seek to continue the ancient ways of the Chamorro people.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_Games">Pacific Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Pacific Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Guam hosted the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Games" title="Pacific Games">Pacific Games</a> in 1975 and 1999. At the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_Games" title="2007 Pacific Games">2007 Games</a>, Guam finished 7th of 22 countries and 14th at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_Games" title="2011 Pacific Games">2011 Games</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Soccer">Soccer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Soccer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_football_team" title="Guam national football team">Guam national football team</a> was founded in 1975 and joined <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> in 1996. <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_football_team" title="Guam national football team">Guam</a> was once considered one of FIFA's weakest teams, and experienced their first victory over a FIFA-registered side in 2009, when they defeated <a href="/wiki/Mongolia_national_football_team" title="Mongolia national football team">Mongolia</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Asian_Cup" title="East Asian Cup">East Asian Cup</a>.</p>
<p>Guam entered the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> Group D. Guam hosted qualifying games on the island for the first time in 2015. During the qualifying round, Guam clinched their first FIFA World Cup Qualifying win by defeating <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_national_football_team" title="Turkmenistan national football team">Turkmenistan</a>. Since then, the team has experienced moderate success in the Qualifying Round with a record of 2–1–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The national team plays at the <a href="/wiki/Guam_National_Football_Stadium" title="Guam National Football Stadium">Guam National Football Stadium</a>, which has a capacity of 1,000. The men's national football team are known as the "matao" team. Matao is the definition of highest level or "noble" class; the matao team have done exceptionally well under the head coach Gary White.</p>
<p>The top football division in Guam is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guam_Men%27s_Soccer_League" title="Guam Men's Soccer League">Guam Men's Soccer League</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rovers_FC_(Guam)" title="Rovers FC (Guam)">Rovers FC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guam_Shipyard" title="Guam Shipyard">Guam Shipyard</a> are the league's most competitive and successful clubs, both have won nine championships in the past years.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_basketball_team" title="Guam national basketball team">Guam national basketball team</a> is traditionally one of the top teams in the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Oceania" title="FIBA Oceania">Oceania region</a> behind <a href="/wiki/Australia_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Australia men's national basketball team">Australia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_basketball_team" title="New Zealand national basketball team">New Zealand</a>.</p>
<p>As of 2015, it is the reigning champion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Games_Basketball_Tournament" title="Pacific Games Basketball Tournament">Pacific Games Basketball Tournament</a>.</p>
<p>Guam is home to various basketball organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Guam_Basketball_Association" title="Guam Basketball Association">GBA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Swimming">Swimming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Swimming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London, <a href="/wiki/Pilar_Shimizu" title="Pilar Shimizu">Pilar Shimizu</a> competed for Guam and placed 42nd in the breaststroke competition.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_union">Rugby union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Rugby union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Guam is represented in <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_rugby_union_team" title="Guam national rugby union team">Guam national rugby union team</a>. The team has never qualified for a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup" title="Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cup</a>. Guam played their first match in 2005, an 8–8 draw with <a href="/wiki/India_national_rugby_union_team" title="India national rugby union team">India</a>. Guam's biggest win was a 74–0 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Brunei_national_rugby_union_team" title="Brunei national rugby union team">Brunei</a> in June 2008.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mixed_martial_arts">Mixed martial arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mixed martial arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UFC" title="UFC">UFC</a> fighter <a href="/wiki/Jon_Tuck" title="Jon Tuck">Jon Tuck</a>, who boasts a professional record of 10 wins and 4 losses, three of those wins while with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UFC" title="UFC">UFC</a>, fights out of Guam.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009_GU_Proof.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1081" data-file-width="1078" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2009_GU_Proof.png/170px-2009_GU_Proof.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2009_GU_Proof.png/255px-2009_GU_Proof.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2009_GU_Proof.png/340px-2009_GU_Proof.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009_GU_Proof.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2009 Guam <a href="/wiki/Quarter_(United_States_coin)" title="Quarter (United States coin)">quarter</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Guam" title="Energy in Guam">Energy in Guam</a></div>
<p>Guam's economy depends primarily on tourism, Department of Defense installations and locally owned businesses. Despite paying no income or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Excise_tax" title="Excise tax">excise tax</a>, it receives large transfer payments from the general revenues of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Department of the Treasury">U.S. federal treasury</a>. Under the provisions of a special law by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a>, it is Guam's treasury rather than the U.S. treasury that receives the federal income taxes paid by local taxpayers (including military and civilian federal employees assigned to Guam).</p>
<p>Lying in the western Pacific, Guam is a popular destination for Japanese tourists. Its tourist hub, <a href="/wiki/Tumon" title="Tumon">Tumon</a>, features over 20 large hotels, a Duty Free Shoppers Galleria, Pleasure Island district, indoor aquarium, Sandcastle <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>–styled shows and other shopping and entertainment venues. It is a relatively short flight from Asia or Australia compared to Hawaii, with hotels and seven public golf courses accommodating over a million tourists per year. Although 75% of the tourists are Japanese, Guam receives a sizable number of tourists from South Korea, the U.S., the Philippines, and Taiwan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Significant sources of revenue include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duty-free" title="Duty-free">duty-free</a> designer shopping outlets, and the American-style malls: <a href="/wiki/Micronesia_Mall" title="Micronesia Mall">Micronesia Mall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guam_Premier_Outlets" title="Guam Premier Outlets">Guam Premier Outlets</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Agana_Shopping_Center" title="Agana Shopping Center">Agana Shopping Center</a>, and the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg/220px-GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg/330px-GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg/440px-GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Terminal at <a href="/wiki/Antonio_B._Won_Pat_International_Airport" title="Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport">Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport</a>. The airport hosts a hub of <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, Guam's largest private-sector employer.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The economy had been stable since 2000 due to increased tourism. It is expected to stabilize with the transfer of U.S. Marine Corps' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3rd_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="3rd Marine Expeditionary Force">3rd Marine Expeditionary Force</a>, currently in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">Okinawa</a>, Japan, (approximately 8,000 Marines, along with their 10,000 dependents), to Guam between 2010 and 2015. In 2003, Guam had a 14% unemployment rate, and the government suffered a $314 million shortfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association" title="Compact of Free Association">Compacts of Free Association</a> between the United States, the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a>, the Republic of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> and the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> accorded the former entities of the <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands</a> a political status of "free association" with the United States. The Compacts give citizens of these island nations generally no restrictions to reside in the United States (also its territories), and many were attracted to Guam due to its proximity, environmental, and cultural familiarity. Over the years, it was claimed by some in Guam that the territory has had to bear the brunt of this agreement in the form of public assistance programs and public education for those from the regions involved, and the federal government should compensate the states and territories affected by this type of migration.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Over the years, Congress had appropriated "Compact Impact" aids to Guam, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a> and Hawaii, and eventually this appropriation was written into each renewed Compact. Some, however, continue to claim the compensation is not enough or that the distribution of actual compensation received is significantly disproportionate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Guam's largest single private sector employer, with about 1,400 jobs, was <a href="/wiki/Continental_Micronesia" title="Continental Micronesia">Continental Micronesia</a>, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> it is now a part of <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, a subsidiary of Chicago-based United Continental Holdings, Inc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the Continental Micronesia annual payroll in Guam was $90 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blairbright_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blairbright-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guam" title="Politics of Guam">Politics of Guam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Voting_in_Guam" title="Voting in Guam">Voting in Guam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Guam" title="Political party strength in Guam">Political party strength in Guam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="217" data-file-width="300" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg/220px-War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park" title="War in the Pacific National Historical Park">War in the Pacific National Historical Park</a> at <a href="/wiki/Asan,_Guam" title="Asan, Guam">Asan</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Guam is governed by a popularly elected governor and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> 15-member legislature, whose members are known as senators. Its judiciary is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Guam" title="Supreme Court of Guam">Supreme Court of Guam</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/District_Court_of_Guam" title="District Court of Guam">District Court of Guam</a> is the court of United States federal jurisdiction in the territory. Guam elects one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delegate_(United_States_Congress)" title="Delegate (United States Congress)">delegate to the United States House of Representatives</a>, currently Democrat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madeleine_Z._Bordallo" title="Madeleine Z. Bordallo">Madeleine Z. Bordallo</a>. The delegate does not have a vote on the final passage of legislation, but is accorded a vote in committee, and the privilege to speak to the House. U.S. citizens in Guam vote in a <a href="/wiki/Straw_poll" title="Straw poll">straw poll</a> for their choice in the U.S. Presidential general election, but since Guam has no votes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College" title="United States Electoral College">Electoral College</a>, the poll has no real effect. However, in sending delegates to the Republican and Democratic national conventions, Guam does have influence in the national presidential race. These delegates are elected by local party <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_primary#Types_of_primaries_and_caucuses" title="United States presidential primary">conventions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rogers-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_status">Political status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Political status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1980s and early 1990s, there was a significant movement in favor of this U.S. territory becoming a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(United_States_insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (United States insular area)">commonwealth</a>, which would give it a level of self-government similar to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a>. However, the federal government rejected the version of a commonwealth that the government of Guam proposed, because its clauses were incompatible with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_Clause" title="Territorial Clause">Territorial Clause</a> (Art. IV, Sec. 3, cl. 2) of the U.S. Constitution. Other movements advocate U.S. statehood for Guam, union with the state of Hawaii, or union with the Northern Mariana Islands as a single territory, or independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 1982 plebiscite, voters indicated interest in seeking commonwealth status.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The island has been considering another non-binding plebiscite on decolonization since 1998. Governor <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Baza_Calvo" title="Eddie Baza Calvo">Eddie Baza Calvo</a> intended to include one during the island's November 2016 elections but it was delayed again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raymundo_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raymundo-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3036" data-file-width="2339" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg/160px-Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg/240px-Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg/320px-Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eddie_Baza_Calvo" title="Eddie Baza Calvo">Eddie Baza Calvo</a>, Governor of Guam</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A Commission on Decolonization was established in 1997 to educate the people of Guam about the various political status options in its relationship with the U.S.: statehood, free association and independence. The group was dormant for some years. In 2013, the Commission began seeking funding to start a public education campaign. There were few subsequent developments until late 2016. In early December 2016, the Commission scheduled a series of education sessions in various villages about the current status of Guam's relationship with the U.S. and the self-determination options that might be considered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raymundo_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Raymundo-41">[41]</a></sup> The Commission's current Executive Director is Edward Alvarez and there are ten members. The group is also expected to release position papers on independence and statehood but the contents have not yet been completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> is in favor of greater self-determination for Guam and other such territories. The UN's <a href="/wiki/Special_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="Special Committee on Decolonization">Special Committee on Decolonization</a> has agreed to endorse the Governor's education plan. The commission's May 2016 report states: "With academics from the University of Guam, [the Commission] was working to create and approve educational materials. The Office of the Governor was collaborating closely with the Commission" in developing educational materials for the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United States <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Interior" title="Department of the Interior">Department of the Interior</a> had approved a $300,000 grant for decolonization education, Edward Alvarez told the United Nations Pacific Regional Seminar in May 2016. "We are hopeful that this might indicate a shift in [United States] policy to its Non-Self-Governing Territories such as Guam, where they will be more willing to engage in discussions about our future and offer true support to help push us towards true self-governances and self-determination."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Villages">Villages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Villages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Villages_of_Guam" title="Villages of Guam">Villages of Guam</a></div>
<p>Guam is divided into nineteen municipalities called villages:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_bases">Military bases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Military bases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_(CVN_76)_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg/220px-US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg/330px-US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg/440px-US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_(CVN_76)_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The aircraft carrier USS <i>Ronald Reagan</i> (CVN 76) enters <a href="/wiki/Apra_Harbor" title="Apra Harbor">Apra Harbor</a> for a scheduled port visit.</div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dd><i>Note: <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Agana" title="Naval Air Station Agana">Naval Air Station Agana</a> has been deactivated.</i> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._military" title="U.S. military">U.S. military</a> maintains jurisdiction over its bases, which cover approximately 39,000 acres (16,000 ha), or 29% of the island's total land area:</p>
<ul>
<li>U.S. <a href="/wiki/Naval_Base_Guam" title="Naval Base Guam">Naval Base Guam</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> – Sumay</li>
<li>U.S. Coast Guard Sector Guam, – Sumay</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andersen_Air_Force_Base" title="Andersen Air Force Base">Andersen Air Force Base</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" title="U.S. Air Force">U.S. Air Force</a> – <a href="/wiki/Yigo" title="Yigo">Yigo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apra_Harbor" title="Apra Harbor">Apra Harbor</a> – Orote peninsula</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Annex" title="Ordnance Annex">Ordnance Annex</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> – South Central Highlands (formerly known as Naval Magazine)</li>
<li>Naval Computer and Telecommunications Station, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> – <a href="/wiki/Barrigada" title="Barrigada">Barrigada</a> and Finegayan</li>
<li>Joint Force Headquarters-Guam, <a href="/wiki/Guam_National_Guard" title="Guam National Guard">Guam National Guard</a> – Radio Barrigada and Fort Juan Muna</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition to on-shore military installations, Guam, along with the rest of the Mariana Islands, is being prepared to be the westernmost military training range for the U.S. Guam is currently viewed as a key military hub that will further allow U.S. military power to be projected via sea and sky.</p>
<p>The U.S. military has proposed building a new aircraft carrier berth on Guam and moving 8,600 Marines, and 9,000 of their dependents, to Guam from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">Okinawa</a>, Japan. Including the required construction workers, this buildup would increase Guam's population by 45%. In a February 2010 letter, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a> sharply criticized these plans because of a water shortfall, sewage problems and the impact on coral reefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> By 2012, these plans had been cut to have only a maximum of 4,800 Marines stationed on the island, two thirds of whom would be there on a rotational basis without their dependents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the proposed increased military presence stemming from the upcoming preparation efforts and relocation efforts of U.S. Marines from Okinawa, Japan to Guam slated to begin in 2010 and last for the next several years thereafter, the amount of total land that the military will control or tenant may grow to or surpass 40% of the entire landmass of Guam.</p>
<p>In January 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Ike_Skelton_National_Defense_Authorization_Act_for_Fiscal_Year_2011" title="Ike Skelton National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2011">Ike Skelton National Defense Authorization Act for FY2011</a> indicated that recent significant events will delay the deadline for realigning U.S. Marine Corps service members and their families from Okinawa to Guam. The transfer may be as late as 2020. In addition, the Defense Authorization Act cut approximately $320 million from the 2011 budget request.</p>
<p>Villagers and the military community are interconnected in many ways. Many villagers serve in the military or are retired. Many active duty personnel and Defense Department civilians also live in the villages outside of the military installation areas. The military and village communities have "adoption" programs where Guam's population and military personnel stationed on Guam perform community service projects.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_and_communications">Transportation and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transportation and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Guam" title="Communications in Guam">Communications in Guam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Guam" title="Transportation in Guam">Transportation in Guam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guam_route_marker_8.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1716" data-file-width="1047" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Guam_route_marker_8.svg/130px-Guam_route_marker_8.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Guam_route_marker_8.svg/195px-Guam_route_marker_8.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Guam_route_marker_8.svg/260px-Guam_route_marker_8.svg.png 2x" width="130"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guam_route_marker_8.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Guam Highway 8 route marker</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of the island has state-of-the-art mobile phone services and high-speed internet widely available through either cable or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DSL" title="DSL">DSL</a>. Guam was added to the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">North American Numbering Plan (NANP)</a> in 1997 (country code 671 became NANP <a href="/wiki/Area_code_671" title="Area code 671">area code 671</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> removing the barrier of high-cost international long-distance calls to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">U.S. mainland</a>.</p>
<p>Guam is also a major hub for submarine cables between the Western U.S., Hawaii, Australia and Asia. Guam currently serves twelve submarine cables, with most continuing to China.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="1547" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg/220px-US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg/330px-US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg/440px-US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cover carried both directions on the first commercial flights between Guam and the United States, October 5–24, 1935.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1899, the local postage stamps were overprinted "Guam" as was done for the other former Spanish colonies, but this was discontinued shortly thereafter and regular U.S. postage stamps have been used ever since. Because Guam is also part of the U.S. Postal System (<a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_abbreviations" title="List of U.S. state abbreviations">postal abbreviation</a>: GU, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">ZIP code range</a>: 96910–96932), mail to Guam from the U.S. mainland is considered domestic and no additional charges are required. Private shipping companies, such as FedEx, UPS, and DHL, however, have no obligation to do so, and do not regard Guam as domestic.</p>
<p>The speed of mail traveling between Guam and the states varies depending on size and time of year. Light, first-class items generally take less than a week to or from the mainland, but larger first-class or Priority items can take a week or two. Fourth-class mail, such as magazines, are transported by sea after reaching Hawaii. Most residents use post office boxes or private mail boxes, although residential delivery is becoming increasingly available. Incoming mail not from the Americas should be addressed to "Guam" instead of "USA" to avoid being routed the long way through the U.S. mainland and possibly charged a higher rate (especially from Asia).</p>
<p>The Commercial Port of Guam is the island's lifeline because most products must be shipped into Guam for consumers. It receives the weekly calls of the Hawaii-based shipping line <a href="/wiki/Matson,_Inc." title="Matson, Inc.">Matson, Inc.</a> whose container ships connect Guam with Honolulu, Hawaii, Los Angeles, California, Oakland, California and Seattle, Washington. The port is also the regional transhipment hub for over 500,000 customers throughout the Micronesian region. The port is the shipping and receiving point for containers designated for the island's U.S. Department of Defense installations, Andersen Air Force Base and Commander, Naval Forces Marianas and eventually the Third Marine Expeditionary Force.</p>
<p>Guam is served by the <a href="/wiki/Antonio_B._Won_Pat_International_Airport" title="Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport">Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport</a>, which is a hub for <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>. The island is outside the United States customs zone so Guam is responsible for establishing and operating its own customs and quarantine agency and jurisdiction. Therefore, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">U.S. Customs and Border Protection</a> only carries immigration (but not customs) functions. Since Guam is under federal immigration jurisdiction, passengers arriving directly from the United States skip immigration and proceed directly to Guam Customs and Quarantine.</p>
<p>However, due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visa_waiver_program#Guam_and_Northern_Mariana_Islands_Visa_Waiver_Program" title="Visa waiver program">Guam and CNMI visa waiver program</a> for certain countries, an eligibility pre-clearance check is carried on Guam for flights to the States. For travel from the Northern Mariana Islands to Guam, a pre-flight passport and visa check is performed before boarding the flight to Guam. On flights from Guam to the Northern Mariana Islands, no immigration check is performed. Traveling between Guam and the States through a foreign point, however, does require a passport.</p>
<p>Most residents travel within Guam using personally owned vehicles. The local government currently outsources the only public bus system (<a href="/wiki/Guam_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="Guam Regional Transit Authority">Guam Regional Transit Authority</a>), and some commercial companies operate buses between tourist-frequented locations</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_issues">Ecological issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ecological issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brown_tree_snake">Brown tree snake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Brown tree snake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="473" data-file-width="643" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg/220px-Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg/330px-Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg/440px-Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_2_USGS_Photograph.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brown_tree_snake" title="Brown tree snake">Brown tree snake</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Believed to be a <a href="/wiki/Stowaway" title="Stowaway">stowaway</a> on a U.S. military transport near the end of World War II, the <a href="/wiki/Brown_tree_snake" title="Brown tree snake">brown tree snake</a> (<i>Boiga irregularis</i>) was accidentally introduced to Guam, which previously had no native species of snake. It nearly eliminated the native bird population. The problem was exacerbated because the snake has no natural predators on the island. The brown tree snake, known locally as the <i>kulebla</i>, is native to northern and eastern coasts of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>. It is slightly venomous, but relatively harmless to human beings; it is nocturnal. Although some studies have suggested a high density of these serpents on Guam, residents rarely see them. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">United States Department of Agriculture</a> has trained detector dogs to keep the snakes out of the island's cargo flow. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> also has dogs that can detect snakes in forested environments around the region's islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the introduction of the brown tree snake, Guam was home to several endemic bird species. Among them were the <a href="/wiki/Guam_rail" title="Guam rail">Guam rail</a> (or <i>ko'ko'</i> bird in Chamorro) and the <a href="/wiki/Guam_flycatcher" title="Guam flycatcher">Guam flycatcher</a>, both common throughout the island. Today the flycatcher is entirely extinct and the Guam rail is extinct in the wild but bred in captivity by the Division of Aquatic and Wildlife Resources. The devastation caused by the snake has been significant over the past several decades. As many as twelve bird species are believed to have been driven to extinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarzluffAngell2007_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarzluffAngell2007-51">[51]</a></sup> According to many elders, ko'ko' birds were common in Guam before World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other bird species threatened by the brown tree snake include the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_crow" title="Mariana crow">Mariana crow</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_swiftlet" title="Mariana swiftlet">Mariana swiftlet</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Micronesian_starling" title="Micronesian starling">Micronesian starling</a>, though populations are present on other islands, including Rota.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarzluffAngell2007_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-MarzluffAngell2007-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Guam is said to have many more insects and 40 times more spiders than neighboring islands, because their natural predators birds are severely diminished, and the forests are almost completely silent due to lack of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birdsong" title="Birdsong">birdsong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="external autonumber" href="http://news.rice.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/0914_SPIDER-b2-big.jpg" rel="nofollow">[1]</a> <a class="external autonumber" href="http://news.rice.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/0914_SPIDER4-webs-big.jpg" rel="nofollow">[2]</a> Forest on Guam swathed in spider webs.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coconut_rhinoceros_beetle">Coconut rhinoceros beetle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Coconut rhinoceros beetle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg/220px-Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg/330px-Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg/440px-Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oryctes_rhinoceros" title="Oryctes rhinoceros">Coconut rhinoceros beetle</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An infestation of the coconut rhinoceros beetle (CRB), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oryctes_rhinoceros" title="Oryctes rhinoceros">Oryctes rhinoceros</a></i>, was detected on Guam on September 12, 2007. CRB is not known to occur in the United States except in <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>. Delimiting surveys performed September 13–25, 2007, indicated that the infestation was limited to Tumon Bay and Faifai Beach, an area of approximately 900 acres (3.6 km<sup>2</sup>). Guam Department of Agriculture (GDA) placed quarantine on all properties within the Tumon area on October 5 and later expanded the quarantine to about 2,500 acres (10 km<sup>2</sup>) on October 25; approximately 0.5 miles (800 m) radius in all directions from all known locations of CRB infestation. CRB is native to Southern Asia and distributed throughout Asia and the Western Pacific including <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>, American Samoa, <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Britain" title="New Britain">New Britain</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Papua_(region)" title="West Papua (region)">West Irian</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Ireland_(island)" title="New Ireland (island)">New Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manus_Island" title="Manus Island">Pak Island and Manus Island</a> (New Guinea), <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocos_(Keeling)_Islands" title="Cocos (Keeling) Islands">Cocos (Keeling) Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Reunion</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_invasive_animal_species">Other invasive animal species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Other invasive animal species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011_Feb,_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan,_10.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1196" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg/170px-2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg/255px-2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg/340px-2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011_Feb,_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan,_10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Adult female <a href="/wiki/Carabao" title="Carabao">carabao</a> and calf</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the seventeenth through nineteenth centuries, the Spanish introduced pigs, dogs, chickens, the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_deer" title="Philippine deer">Philippine deer</a> (<i>Rusa mariannus</i>), <a href="/wiki/Black_francolin" title="Black francolin">black francolins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carabao" title="Carabao">carabao</a> (a subspecies of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_buffalo" title="Domestic buffalo">water buffalo</a>), which have cultural significance. Herds of carabao obstruct military base operations and harm native ecosystems. After birth control and adoption efforts were ineffective, the U.S. military began culling the herds in 2002 leading to organized protests from island residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other introduced species include <a href="/wiki/Cane_toad" title="Cane toad">cane toads</a> imported in 1937, the <a href="/wiki/Achatina_achatina" title="Achatina achatina">giant African snail</a> (an agricultural pest introduced during World War II by Japanese occupation troops) and more recently frog species which could threaten crops in addition to providing additional food for the <a href="/wiki/Brown_tree_snake" title="Brown tree snake">brown tree snake</a> population. Reports of loud chirping frogs native to Puerto Rico and known as <a href="/wiki/Common_coqu%C3%AD" title="Common coquí">coquí</a>, that may have arrived from Hawaii, have led to fears that the noise could threaten Guam's tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Guam has no native amphibian species, but now a total of eight amphibian species has been established in Guam. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Litoria_fallax" title="Litoria fallax">Litoria fallax</a></i> (native to the eastern coast of Australia) has been present in Guam since 1968, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhinella_marina" title="Rhinella marina">Rhinella marina</a></i> (the cane toad) was brought to the island in 1937. The other 6 amphibian species, namely <i><a href="/wiki/Hylarana_guentheri" title="Hylarana guentheri">Hylarana guentheri</a></i> (native to mainland Asia), <i><a href="/wiki/Microhyla_pulchra" title="Microhyla pulchra">Microhyla pulchra</a></i> (native to mainland Asia), <i><a href="/wiki/Polypedates_braueri" title="Polypedates braueri">Polypedates braueri</a></i> (endemic to Taiwan), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleutherodactylus_planirostris" title="Eleutherodactylus planirostris">Eleutherodactylus planirostris</a></i> (native to the Caribbean), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fejervarya_cancrivora" title="Fejervarya cancrivora">Fejervarya cancrivora</a></i> (the Guam variety being most closely related to <i>F. cancrivora</i> found in Taiwan), and <i><a href="/wiki/Fejervarya_limnocharis" title="Fejervarya limnocharis">Fejervarya limnocharis</a></i> (native to Southeast Asia), have been in Guam since 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Many species were likely inadvertently introduced via shipping cargo, especially from Taiwan, mainland China, and Southeast Asia.</p>
<p>Introduced feral pigs and deer, over-hunting, and habitat loss from human development are also major factors in the decline and loss of Guam's native plants and animals.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Threats_to_indigenous_plants">Threats to indigenous plants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Threats to indigenous plants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Invading animal species are not the only threat to Guam's native flora. Tinangaja, a <a href="/wiki/Plant_virus" title="Plant virus">virus</a> affecting coconut palms, was first observed on the island in 1917 when <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> production was still a major part of Guam's economy. Though coconut plantations no longer exist on the island, the dead and infected trees that have resulted from the epidemic are seen throughout the forests of Guam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the past century, the dense forests of northern Guam have been largely replaced by thick <i>tangan-tangan</i> brush (<i><a href="/wiki/Leucaena_leucocephala" title="Leucaena leucocephala">Leucaena leucocephala</a></i>). Much of Guam's foliage was lost during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. In 1947, the U.S. military is thought to have planted tangan-tangan by seeding the island from the air to prevent <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a>. Tangan-tangan was present on the island before 1905.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>In southern Guam, non-native grass species dominate much of the landscape. Although the colorful and impressive flame tree (<i><a href="/wiki/Delonix_regia" title="Delonix regia">Delonix regia</a></i>) is found throughout the Marianas, the tree on Guam has been largely decimated.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildfires">Wildfires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Wildfires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guam_Grassland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="150" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6f/Guam_Grassland.jpg" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guam_Grassland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Guam's grassland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">Wildfires</a> plague the forested areas of Guam every <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a> despite the island's humid climate. Most fires are caused by humans with 80% resulting from arson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Poachers often start fires to attract deer to the new growth. Invasive grass species that rely on fire as part of their natural life cycle grow in many regularly burned areas. Grasslands and "barrens" have replaced previously forested areas leading to greater soil erosion. During the rainy season, sediment is carried by the heavy rains into the <a href="/wiki/Fena_Lake" title="Fena Lake">Fena Lake</a> Reservoir and <a href="/wiki/Ugum_River" title="Ugum River">Ugum River</a>, leading to water quality problems for southern Guam. Eroded silt also destroys the marine life in reefs around the island. Soil stabilization efforts by volunteers and forestry workers (planting trees) have had little success in preserving natural habitats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aquatic_preserves">Aquatic preserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Aquatic preserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tumon_Beach.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1197" data-file-width="1708" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Tumon_Beach.JPG/220px-Tumon_Beach.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Tumon_Beach.JPG/330px-Tumon_Beach.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Tumon_Beach.JPG/440px-Tumon_Beach.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tumon_Beach.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Having previously experienced extensive <a href="/wiki/Dredging" title="Dredging">dredging</a>, Tumon Bay is now a marine wildlife preserve.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Efforts have been made to protect Guam's coral reef habitats from pollution, eroded silt and overfishing, problems that have led to decreased fish populations. (Since Guam is a significant vacation spot for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scuba_diver" title="Scuba diver">scuba divers</a>, this is important.) In recent years, the Department of Agriculture, Division of Aquatic and Wildlife Resources has established several new marine preserves where fish populations are monitored by biologists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Before adopting <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a> standards, portions of Tumon Bay were dredged by the hotel chains to provide a better experience for hotel guests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Tumon Bay has since been made into a preserve. A federal <a href="/wiki/Guam_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Guam National Wildlife Refuge">Guam National Wildlife Refuge</a> in northern Guam protects the decimated <a href="/wiki/Sea_turtle" title="Sea turtle">sea turtle</a> population in addition to a small colony of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mariana_fruit_bats" title="Mariana fruit bats">Mariana fruit bats</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harvest of sea turtle eggs was a common occurrence on Guam before World War II. The <a href="/wiki/Green_sea_turtle" title="Green sea turtle">green sea turtle</a> (<i>Chelonia mydas</i>) was harvested legally on Guam before August 1978, when it was listed as threatened under the Endangered Species Act. The <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_sea_turtle" title="Hawksbill sea turtle">hawksbill sea turtle</a> (<i>Eretmochelys imbricata</i>) has been on the endangered list since 1970. In an effort to ensure protection of sea turtles on Guam, routine sightings are counted during aerial surveys and nest sites are recorded and monitored for hatchlings.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG/220px-University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG/330px-University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG/440px-University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The central campus at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Guam" title="University of Guam">University of Guam</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Guam" title="University of Guam">University of Guam</a> (UOG) and <a href="/wiki/Guam_Community_College" title="Guam Community College">Guam Community College</a>, both fully accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="Western Association of Schools and Colleges">Western Association of Schools and Colleges</a>, offer courses in higher education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> UOG is a member of the exclusive group of only 76 <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land-grant institutions</a> in the entire United States. <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_University" title="Pacific Islands University">Pacific Islands University</a> is a small Christian liberal arts institution nationally accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Transnational_Association_of_Christian_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Transnational Association of Christian Colleges and Schools">Transnational Association of Christian Colleges and Schools</a>. They offer courses at both the undergraduate and graduate levels.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_schools">Primary and secondary schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Guam" title="List of schools in Guam">List of schools in Guam</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guam_Department_of_Education" title="Guam Department of Education">Guam Department of Education</a> serves the entire island of Guam. In 2000, 32,000 students attended Guam's public schools. Guam Public Schools have struggled with problems such as high dropout rates and poor test scores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merrow_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merrow-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-State-68">[68]</a></sup> Guam's educational system has always faced unique challenges as a small community located 6,000 miles (9,700 km) from the U.S. mainland with a very diverse student body including many students who come from backgrounds without traditional American education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peabody_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peabody-69">[69]</a></sup> An economic downturn in Guam since the mid-1990s has compounded the problems in schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guam_Legislature_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guam_Legislature-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before September 1997, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Defense" title="U.S. Department of Defense">U.S. Department of Defense</a> partnered with Guam Board of Education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In September 1997, the DoDEA opened its own schools for children of military personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Defense_Education_Activity" title="Department of Defense Education Activity">DoDEA</a> schools, which also serve children of some federal civilian employees, had an attendance of 2,500 in 2000. DoDEA Guam operates three elementary/middle schools and one high school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DODEA_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-DODEA-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries">Public libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Public libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Guam_Public_Library_System" title="Guam Public Library System">Guam Public Library System</a> operates the Nieves M. Flores Memorial Library in <a href="/wiki/Hag%C3%A5t%C3%B1a" title="Hagåtña">Hagåtña</a> and five branch libraries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Government of Guam maintains the island's main health care facility, <a href="/wiki/Guam_Memorial_Hospital" title="Guam Memorial Hospital">Guam Memorial Hospital</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamuning,_Guam" title="Tamuning, Guam">Tamuning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> U.S. board certified doctors and dentists practice in all specialties. In addition, the U.S. Naval Hospital in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agana_Heights,_Guam" title="Agana Heights, Guam">Agana Heights</a> serves active-duty members and dependents of the military community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> There is one subscriber-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_ambulance" title="Air ambulance">air ambulance</a> located on the island, CareJet, which provides emergency patient transportation across Guam and surrounding islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> A private hospital, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guam_Regional_Medical_City&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guam Regional Medical City (page does not exist)">Guam Regional Medical City</a> opened its doors in early 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRMC_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-GRMC-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Film-making">Film-making</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Film-making">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Over the years, a number of films have been shot on Guam, including <i>Shiro's Head</i> (directed by the Muna brothers) and the government-funded <i><a href="/wiki/Max_Havoc:_Curse_of_the_Dragon" title="Max Havoc: Curse of the Dragon">Max Havoc: Curse of the Dragon</a></i> (2004). Although set on Guam, <i><a href="/wiki/No_Man_Is_an_Island_(film)" title="No Man Is an Island (film)">No Man Is an Island</a></i> (1962) was not shot there, but in the Republic of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
